Hajj — Pilgrimage

Definition of Hajj: Linguistic and Legal
Opening definition of hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definitions of hajj and identify the element of veneration (ta'dhim) that distinguishes it from ordinary travel.

Core Idea
Hajj is linguistically 'intent' and legally 'intent to the Kaaba with veneration to perform a great pillar'.

The Book of Hajj opens with its definition. Understanding this definition is crucial because it establishes hajj as a distinct act of worship requiring both physical intent and spiritual reverence. This definition also sets the foundation for all subsequent rules of hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definition
The text states: 'الحج في اللغة: عبارة عن القصد'. So hajj linguistically means 'intent' (qasd).
The general meaning of 'qasd' is any kind of intention or aim.
2
Identify the legal definition
The shar'i definition adds three elements: (1) the object: the Kaaba (al-bayt), (2) the manner: with veneration (ala wajh al-ta'dhim), and (3) the purpose: to perform a great pillar of religion (li-ada' rukn min al-din 'azim).
Veneration (ta'dhim) is key—it implies the rites of hajj are performed out of reverence, not merely habit.
3
Understand the implication
This definition immediately classifies hajj as a high-level obligation ('great pillar'), which the commentator later confirms is fard muḥkam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحج واجب.
كتاب الحج
الحج في اللغة: عبارة عن القصد.
وفي الشرع : عبارة عن قصد البيت على وجه التعظيم؛ لأداء ركن من الدين عظيم.
- والعبادات ثلاث:
بدني محض، كالصلاة والصوم.
ومالي مَحْضُ، كالزكاة.
ومركب منهما، وهو الحج.
فلما فرغ من البدني والمالي: شرع في المركب.
قال رحمه الله : (الحج: واجب) : أي فرضٌ مُحكم.
وإنما ذكره بلفظ : الوجوب؛ لأن الواجب أعم؛ لأن كل فرض: واجب، وليس كل واجب فرضاً.
والمشروعات أربعة : فريضة، وواجب، وسُنَّةٌ، ونافلة.
Hajj is obligatory. Book of Hajj. Hajj linguistically means 'intent'. Legally, it means 'intent to the House (Kaaba) in a manner of veneration, to perform a great pillar of the religion.' Acts of worship are three: purely bodily, like prayer and fasting; purely financial, like zakat; and composite of both, which is Hajj. When he finished with the bodily and financial, he began with the composite. He (the author) said: 'Hajj is wajib' meaning a firmly established fard. He only mentioned it with the term 'wujub' because wajib is more general, for every fard is wajib, but not every wajib is fard. The legislated matters are four: fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafilah.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of Hajj with the foundational definition and classification. The author first states that Hajj is wajib (obligatory). He then provides the linguistic and technical definitions of Hajj: linguistically 'intent', technically 'intent to the Kaaba with veneration to perform a great religious pillar'. He categorizes acts of worship into three types: purely bodily (salah, sawm), purely financial (zakat), and composite of both (Hajj), explaining that since the author (al-Quduri) completed discussion of the bodily and financial acts, he now proceeds to the composite. The commentator explains why the matn uses 'wajib' instead of 'fard': because in the Hanafi school, 'wajib' is a broader category that includes 'fard' but also includes obligations established by non-definitive evidence. Every fard is wajib, but not every wajib is fard. The legislated matters (al-mashru'at) are four levels: fard (established by definitive proof), wajib (established by probable proof), sunnah (recommended), and nafilah (supererogatory). This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh for understanding the degree of obligation and the consequence of leaving an act.

Key Terms
حج (hajj): Intent to the Kaaba with veneration to perform a great pillar of religion
واجب (wājib): A legal obligation that is established by probable (zanni) evidence; a broader category that includes fard
فرض (farḍ): A legal obligation established by definitive (qat'i) evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the legal definition of hajj includes which of the following elements?
A) Intent + Veneration + Performing a great pillar
B) Intent + Financial cost
C) Veneration + Travel
D) Intent + Pilgrimage rules

Key Takeaway
Hajj is defined as intent to the Kaaba with veneration to perform a great pillar—this sets it apart from ordinary travel and establishes it as a major obligatory worship.

Categories of Acts of Worship: Bodily, Financial, and Composite
Classification of acts of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorize acts of worship into three types and explain why the author discusses hajj after prayer, fasting, and zakat.

Core Idea
Acts of worship are three: purely bodily, purely financial, and composite of both; hajj is the composite.

The author provides a typology of worship that helps organize the fiqh curriculum. After completing the purely bodily (salah, sawm) and purely financial (zakat) acts, he begins the composite act—hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The text says: 'والعبادات ثلاث: بدني محض، كالصلاة والصوم. ومالي محض، كالزكاة. ومركب منهما، وهو الحج.'
Bodily: requires only physical exertion; Financial: requires only wealth; Composite: requires both.
2
Note the author's transition
The phrase 'فلما فرغ من البدني والمالي: شرع في المركب' shows that al-Quduri arranged his Mukhtasar starting with pure bodily acts (Books of Prayer and Fasting), then pure financial (Book of Zakat), and now composite (Book of Hajj).
This is a pedagogical ordering from simple to more complex.
3
Understand the composite nature
Hajj requires both physical effort (travel, standing, circumambulation) and financial expenditure (expenses, sacrifice). It is the only act of worship among the five pillars that combines both elements.
This characteristic influences the conditions of obligation (istita'ah includes both physical and financial ability).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحج واجب.
كتاب الحج
الحج في اللغة: عبارة عن القصد.
وفي الشرع : عبارة عن قصد البيت على وجه التعظيم؛ لأداء ركن من الدين عظيم.
- والعبادات ثلاث:
بدني محض، كالصلاة والصوم.
ومالي مَحْضُ، كالزكاة.
ومركب منهما، وهو الحج.
فلما فرغ من البدني والمالي: شرع في المركب.
قال رحمه الله : (الحج: واجب) : أي فرضٌ مُحكم.
وإنما ذكره بلفظ : الوجوب؛ لأن الواجب أعم؛ لأن كل فرض: واجب، وليس كل واجب فرضاً.
والمشروعات أربعة : فريضة، وواجب، وسُنَّةٌ، ونافلة.
Hajj is obligatory. Book of Hajj. Hajj linguistically means 'intent'. Legally, it means 'intent to the House (Kaaba) in a manner of veneration, to perform a great pillar of the religion.' Acts of worship are three: purely bodily, like prayer and fasting; purely financial, like zakat; and composite of both, which is Hajj. When he finished with the bodily and financial, he began with the composite. He (the author) said: 'Hajj is wajib' meaning a firmly established fard. He only mentioned it with the term 'wujub' because wajib is more general, for every fard is wajib, but not every wajib is fard. The legislated matters are four: fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafilah.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of Hajj with the foundational definition and classification. The author first states that Hajj is wajib (obligatory). He then provides the linguistic and technical definitions of Hajj: linguistically 'intent', technically 'intent to the Kaaba with veneration to perform a great religious pillar'. He categorizes acts of worship into three types: purely bodily (salah, sawm), purely financial (zakat), and composite of both (Hajj), explaining that since the author (al-Quduri) completed discussion of the bodily and financial acts, he now proceeds to the composite. The commentator explains why the matn uses 'wajib' instead of 'fard': because in the Hanafi school, 'wajib' is a broader category that includes 'fard' but also includes obligations established by non-definitive evidence. Every fard is wajib, but not every wajib is fard. The legislated matters (al-mashru'at) are four levels: fard (established by definitive proof), wajib (established by probable proof), sunnah (recommended), and nafilah (supererogatory). This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh for understanding the degree of obligation and the consequence of leaving an act.

Key Terms
عبادات (ibādāt): Acts of worship classified into three types

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many categories of acts of worship are mentioned in the passage?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Hajj is unique among the pillars as it combines bodily and financial elements, explaining its placement after the bodily and financial acts in fiqh manuals.

The Hanafi Distinction Between Fard and Wajib
Clarification of fard vs wajib and listing of mashru'at

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish fard from wajib in Hanafi fiqh and list the four levels of mashru'at.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, every fard is wajib, but not every wajib is fard; fard is based on conclusive evidence, wajib on probable evidence.

The author states 'Hajj is wajib', but the commentator clarifies that it means 'fard muḥkam'. This leads to a crucial usul principle: the Hanafi classification of obligations into fard and wajib, and the broader four categories of legislated matters.

Guided Path
1
Note the author's wording
The matn says 'الحج: واجب'. The commentator explains that this means 'فرض محكم' (a firmly established fard).
2
Understand why 'wajib' was used
The commentator says: 'وإنما ذكره بلفظ الوجوب؛ لأن الواجب أعم'. Wajib is the broader category; it includes fard. So using 'wajib' to mean fard is permissible because fard is a subset of wajib.
In Hanafi usul, fard is defined as obligation from qat'i (definitive) evidence, while wajib is from zanni (probable) evidence.
3
Learn the Hanafi hierarchy of obligations
The text then lists the four mashru'at: 'فريضة، وواجب، وسنة، ونافلة'. Fard is proven by qat'i evidence, wajib by zanni, sunnah is recommended, nafilah is supererogatory.
This classification affects consequences: omitting a fard invalidates the act (if rukn) or requires compensation, omitting a wajib requires compensation (sajda sahw/dam), omitting sunnah is less severe.
4
Apply to hajj
Since hajj is established by Quran (3:97) which is qat'i, it is fard. So the commentator clarifies that the author's 'wajib' is actually fard in this context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحج واجب.
كتاب الحج
الحج في اللغة: عبارة عن القصد.
وفي الشرع : عبارة عن قصد البيت على وجه التعظيم؛ لأداء ركن من الدين عظيم.
- والعبادات ثلاث:
بدني محض، كالصلاة والصوم.
ومالي مَحْضُ، كالزكاة.
ومركب منهما، وهو الحج.
فلما فرغ من البدني والمالي: شرع في المركب.
قال رحمه الله : (الحج: واجب) : أي فرضٌ مُحكم.
وإنما ذكره بلفظ : الوجوب؛ لأن الواجب أعم؛ لأن كل فرض: واجب، وليس كل واجب فرضاً.
والمشروعات أربعة : فريضة، وواجب، وسُنَّةٌ، ونافلة.
Hajj is obligatory. Book of Hajj. Hajj linguistically means 'intent'. Legally, it means 'intent to the House (Kaaba) in a manner of veneration, to perform a great pillar of the religion.' Acts of worship are three: purely bodily, like prayer and fasting; purely financial, like zakat; and composite of both, which is Hajj. When he finished with the bodily and financial, he began with the composite. He (the author) said: 'Hajj is wajib' meaning a firmly established fard. He only mentioned it with the term 'wujub' because wajib is more general, for every fard is wajib, but not every wajib is fard. The legislated matters are four: fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafilah.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of Hajj with the foundational definition and classification. The author first states that Hajj is wajib (obligatory). He then provides the linguistic and technical definitions of Hajj: linguistically 'intent', technically 'intent to the Kaaba with veneration to perform a great religious pillar'. He categorizes acts of worship into three types: purely bodily (salah, sawm), purely financial (zakat), and composite of both (Hajj), explaining that since the author (al-Quduri) completed discussion of the bodily and financial acts, he now proceeds to the composite. The commentator explains why the matn uses 'wajib' instead of 'fard': because in the Hanafi school, 'wajib' is a broader category that includes 'fard' but also includes obligations established by non-definitive evidence. Every fard is wajib, but not every wajib is fard. The legislated matters (al-mashru'at) are four levels: fard (established by definitive proof), wajib (established by probable proof), sunnah (recommended), and nafilah (supererogatory). This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh for understanding the degree of obligation and the consequence of leaving an act.

Key Terms
فريضة (farīḍah): A fard obligation (from qat'i evidence)
سنة (sunnah): Recommended, non-obligatory act
نافلة (nāfilah): Supererogatory act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, how many categories of mashru'at are there?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, fard is a subset of wajib; hajj is fard, and the four mashru'at are fard, wajib, sunnah, nafilah.

Hajj is Fard: Obligation, Classification, and Timing Dispute
Establishes obligation of Hajj, defines fiqh categories, and discusses immediate vs delayed performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between fard and wajib in Hanafi fiqh and explain the internal Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of Hajj (fawr vs tarakhi).

Core Idea
Hajj is fard, proven by the Quran; but Hanafi imams differ: must it be performed immediately or can it be delayed?

In this lesson, we examine the obligation of Hajj as presented in Al-Jawharah al-Nayrah, a commentary on Al-Quduri. The passage clarifies the Hanafi classification of fard vs wajib, establishes the Quranic proof for Hajj, and then delves into an intra-Hanafi debate: is the obligation immediate (fawr) or delayed (tarakhi)? This dispute affects when a Muslim becomes sinful for delaying Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that Hajj is 'wajib' which is further clarified as fard muḥkam (firmly established obligation). Note the Hanafi distinction: fard vs wajib.
The term 'wajib' in the matn is general; the commentary specifies it is fard.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse (3:97) is cited as the primary proof for the obligation.
A hadith is also mentioned for the timing dispute.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The preposition 'ala in the verse indicates obligation per Hanafi usul (the principle 'ala li al-wujub).
This is a key principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage presents the internal Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf (fawr) and Muhammad (tarakhi).
Both agree on consensus for immediate if death is feared.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The commentator sides with Abu Yusuf by providing a hadith, making the mufta bihi fawr (immediate).
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحج في اللغة: عبارة عن القصد. وفي الشرع : عبارة عن قصد البيت على وجه التعظيم؛ لأداء ركن من الدين عظيم.
- والعبادات ثلاث:
بدني محض، كالصلاة والصوم.
ومالي مَحْضُ، كالزكاة.
ومركب منهما، وهو الحج.
فلما فرغ من البدني والمالي: شرع في المركب.
قال رحمه الله : (الحج: واجب) : أي فرضٌ مُحكم.
وإنما ذكره بلفظ : الوجوب؛ لأن الواجب أعم؛ لأن كل فرض: واجب، وليس كل واجب فرضاً.
والمشروعات أربعة : فريضة، وواجب، وسُنَّةٌ، ونافلة.
فالفريضة : ما ثبت بدليل قطعي لا شبهة فيه كالكتاب والخبر المتواتر. والواجب : ما ثبت بدليل فيه شبهة، كخبر الواحد.
والسنَّة : هي طريقة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، أمرنا بإحيائها. والنافلة هي ما شرعت لتحصيل الثواب، ولا يلحق تاركها مأثم، ولا عقاب.
فالحج فرض مُحكم، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ . الآية. آل عمران/۹۷
وهل وجوبه على الفور أم على التراخي؟
فعند أبي يوسف: على الفور ؛ لأنه يختص بوقت خاص، والموت في سنة واحدة غير نادر.
وعند محمد : على التراخي ؛ لأنه وظيفة العمر.
والخلاف فيما إذا كان غالب ظنه السلامة، أما إذا كان غالب ظنه الموت، إما بسبب المرض أو الهرم فإنه يتضيق عليه الوجوب، إجماعاً. فعند أبي يوسف: لا يباح له التأخير عند الإمكان، فإن أخره: كان آثماً ، وحجته: قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : من ملك زاداً وراحلة تبلغه إلى بيت الله الحرام، فلم يحج فلا عليه أن يموت يهودياً أو نصرانياً (١).
Hajj in language: expression of intention. And in Sacred Law: expression of intending the House (Kaaba) in a manner of veneration; to perform a great pillar of the religion.
- And acts of worship are three:
Purely physical, like prayer and fasting.
And purely financial, like zakat.
And composite of both, which is Hajj.
When he finished from the physical and financial, he began the composite.
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: "Hajj: is obligatory (wajib)" i.e. a firmly established fard.
And he only mentioned it with the word wujub because wajib is more general; because every fard is wajib, but not every wajib is fard.
And the legislated matters are four: fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafl.
So fard: what is established by a definitive proof without any doubt, like the Book and the mutawatir report. And wajib: what is established by a proof containing some doubt, like the report of a single narrator.
And sunnah: it is the way of the Prophet (peace be upon him), which we are commanded to revive. And nafl: it is legislated to attain reward, and the one who abandons it incurs no sin or punishment.
So Hajj is a firmly established fard. Allah Almighty said: "And for Allah upon the people is pilgrimage to the House..." the verse. (Al-Imran/97)
And is its obligation immediate or delayed?
According to Abu Yusuf: immediate, because it is specific to a particular time, and death within one year is not rare.
And according to Muhammad: delayed, because it is a function of a lifetime.
And the difference is when his predominant assumption is safety; but if his predominant assumption is death, either due to illness or old age, then the obligation becomes immediate, by consensus. According to Abu Yusuf: it is not permissible for him to delay when possible; if he delays, he is sinful. His evidence is his statement (peace be upon him): "Whoever possesses provisions and a mount that takes him to the Sacred House of Allah and does not perform Hajj, let him die as a Jew or a Christian."
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayrah is an expansion of the Quduri matn's opening of Kitab al-Hajj: "Al-Hajj: wajib." The commentator begins with lexical and technical definitions of Hajj, then categorizes worship into three types: physical, financial, and composite. Since the author had previously covered physical (salah, sawm) and financial (zakat), he now turns to the composite act, Hajj.

The matn uses the term 'wajib' for Hajj, but the commentator clarifies that this means 'fard muḥkam' (firmly established obligation). He explains the Hanafi distinction: fard is proven by a qati' (definitive) dalil like the Quran or mutawatir hadith; wajib is proven by a zanni (probable) dalil like ahad hadith. Every fard is wajib, but not every wajib is fard (a unique Hanafi distinction not shared by other schools). The four categories of legislated acts are fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafl.

After proving the obligation with the Quranic verse (3:97), the commentator raises the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the timing: immediate (fawr) or delayed (tarakhi). Abu Yusuf argues for immediacy because Hajj is time-specific (the months of Hajj) and death can occur any year. Muhammad argues for delay because Hajj is a once-in-a-lifetime duty that can be performed at any time. Both agree that if one fears death (due to illness or old age), the obligation becomes immediate by consensus. The commentator then quotes a hadith (though with chain issues noted) to support Abu Yusuf's view.

Key Terms
فريضة (farīḍah): An obligation established by a definitive proof (dalil qat'i) such as the Quran or mutawatir hadith.
واجب (wājib): An obligation established by a proof containing doubt (dalil zanni), such as ahad hadith.
سنة (sunnah): The way of the Prophet which we are commanded to revive; omitting it is not sinful.
فور (fawr): Immediate performance upon meeting conditions; delaying is sinful.
تراخي (tarākhī): Delayed performance; it is permissible to postpone until later in life.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the difference between fard and wajib?
A) Fard is proven by a definitive proof; wajib by a probable proof.
B) Fard is obligatory; wajib is recommended.
C) Wajib is proven by the Quran; fard by hadith.
D) They are synonymous.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is a fard proven by the Quran; in the Hanafi school, the relied-upon view is that it must be performed immediately (fawr) upon meeting conditions.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Immediate vs. Deferred Obligation of Hajj: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of Hajj obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the timing of Hajj (fawr vs tarakhi), explain the proofs for each, and identify the mufta bihi (operative) ruling.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory immediately (fawr): delaying without excuse incurs sin per the relied-upon Hanafi view.

This passage from 'Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira' discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the obligation of Hajj must be performed immediately or can be deferred. The base text (Mukhtasar al-Quduri) establishes Hajj as a definitive obligation; the commentator expands on the timing. Two great Hanafi imams, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differ, and each brings textual evidence. Understanding this dispute clarifies the practical ruling for a Muslim who becomes capable of Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The core question: Once Hajj becomes obligatory (through istita'ah), must it be performed in the earliest possible season, or can it be delayed to a later year?
The dispute does not question the obligation itself, only its timing.
2
State each imam's position
Abu Yusuf: immediate (fawr) – sin for delaying. Muhammad: deferred (tarakhi) – no sin as long as performed before death. Abu Hanifa agrees with Abu Yusuf.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both are within the school.
3
Examine the proofs
Abu Yusuf cites the hadith threatening death as a Jew/Christian for delaying despite ability. Muhammad cites the Prophet's own delay of Hajj from the 6th to the 10th year after Hijrah.
Both proofs are from Sunnah.
4
Analyze the rebuttal
Abu Yusuf responds that the Prophet had divine knowledge of his lifespan, so his delay is not a precedent for us who lack such assurance.
This rebuttal preserves the force of the hadith.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is fawr (immediate), supported by Abu Hanifa and later Hanafi authorities. A delay without valid excuse is sinful.
However, if one fears death due to illness or old age, all agree it becomes urgent immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالحج فرض مُحكم، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ . الآية. آل عمران/۹۷ وهل وجوبه على الفور أم على التراخي؟ فعند أبي يوسف: على الفور ؛ لأنه يختص بوقت خاص، والموت في سنة واحدة غير نادر. وعند محمد : على التراخي ؛ لأنه وظيفة العمر. والخلاف فيما إذا كان غالب ظنه السلامة، أما إذا كان غالب ظنه الموت، إما بسبب المرض أو الهرم فإنه يتضيق عليه الوجوب، إجماعاً. فعند أبي يوسف: لا يباح له التأخير عند الإمكان، فإن أخره: كان آثماً ، وحجته: قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : من ملك زاداً وراحلة تبلغه إلى بيت الله الحرام، فلم يحج فلا عليه أن يموت يهودياً أو نصرانياً (١). وحُجَّةٌ محمد: أن الله تعالى فَرَضَه سنةَ ست، وحج رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سنة عشر ، ولو كان وجوبه على الفور: لم يؤخره. والجواب لأبي يوسف : أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قد علم بطريق الوحي أنه يعيش إلى أن يؤديه، فكان آمنا من فواته. (١) سنن الترمذي ،(۸۱۲)، والحديث له عدة طرق وفيها مقال، ينظر البدر المنير ١٠٥/١٥ ، التعريف والإخبار ١٦٣/٤ ، نصب الراية ٤١٠/٤.
Hajj is a definitive obligation. Allah Most High says: 'And due to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House' [Al 'Imran 97]. Is its obligation immediate or deferred? According to Abu Yusuf: immediate, because it is specific to a special time and death within one year is not rare. According to Muhammad: deferred, because it is a lifelong duty. The disagreement is when one's dominant presumption is safety. If the dominant presumption is death due to illness or old age, then the obligation becomes urgent by consensus. According to Abu Yusuf, it is not permitted to delay when possible; if one delays, he is sinful. His proof is the hadith: 'Whoever possesses provisions and a mount that reaches the House of Allah but does not perform Hajj, then let him die as a Jew or a Christian.' (1) Muhammad's proof: Allah obligated it in the year six (AH), and the Prophet ﷺ performed Hajj in year ten; if it were immediate, he would not have delayed it. Abu Yusuf's response: The Prophet ﷺ knew through revelation that he would live to perform it, so he was safe from missing it.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the obligation of Hajj is immediate (fawr) or deferred (tarakhi). The base text (Mukhtasar al-Quduri) likely stated it as fard, and the commentator expands on the disagreement. Abu Yusuf argues for fawr because Hajj is tied to a specific season (the months of Hajj), and delaying risks death. He cites a hadith threatening severe consequences for delaying. Muhammad argues for tarakhi because Hajj is a once-in-a-lifetime duty that can be performed any year; he points to the Prophet's delay from year 6 to year 10. Abu Yusuf counters that the Prophet had divine assurance of his lifespan. The dispute applies only when one expects safety; if one fears death, all agree it becomes urgent. The Hanafi mufta bihi is generally the view of Abu Yusuf (and Abu Hanifa) that Hajj is immediate.

Key Terms
الفور (al-fawr): Immediate obligation; must be performed as soon as possible.
التراخي (al-tarākhī): Deferred obligation; may be delayed as long as one intends to perform it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is the ruling if a person delays Hajj for one year without excuse after becoming able?
A) The delay is permissible because the obligation is deferred.
B) The delay is sinful because the obligation is immediate.
C) The delay is only makruh (disliked).
D) The Hajj becomes invalid if not done immediately.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's preferred view is that Hajj must be performed as soon as possible after becoming able; delaying without excuse is sinful.

Freedom as a Condition for Hajj Obligation
Explaining why slaves are not obligated to perform Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why freedom is a condition for the obligation of Hajj in the Hanafi school and explain the evidence from hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
A slave is not obligated to perform Hajj because he lacks wealth and his master's rights take precedence.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayirah elaborates on the condition of freedom (hurriyyah) for the obligation of Hajj. The author explains that a slave is not among 'the people' addressed in the Qur'anic verse, and supports this with a hadith and a rational analogy to prayer and fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Condition
The base text states 'upon the free', indicating that freedom is a condition for Hajj obligation. Note that Hajj is not required from slaves.
The plural 'free' hints at the communal nature of Hajj.
2
Examine the Hadith Proof
The Prophet ﷺ said that a slave's Hajj before freedom does not fulfill the obligatory Hajj. This shows that the obligation only attaches to free persons.
The hadith is considered weak but is accepted in meaning.
3
Analyze the Qiyas with Prayer and Fasting
A hypothetical objection asks why prayer and fasting are obligatory on slaves but not Hajj. The answer: prayer and fasting do not require wealth and are short, whereas Hajj requires money and long absence.
This qiyas reveals the effective cause (ʿillah): need for wealth and prolonged time.
4
Understand the Underlying Rationale
The slave owns nothing (Quran 16:75) and his master's rights over his service would be lost for a long period. Thus, the slave's obligation is suspended until freedom.
This rationale protects the master's rights and recognizes the slave's incapacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (على الأحرار). إنما ذكره بلفظ الجمع ؛ لأنه لا يؤدى بمنفرد، بل يُقام بجمع عظيم، وإليه الإشارة بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ . آل عمران / ۹۷ وإنما شرط الحرية؛ لأن العبد ليس من أهله، قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «أيما عبد حج ولو عشر حِجَج ثم أعتق: فعليه حجة الإسلام (۱). فإن قيل: ما الفرق بين الصلاة والصوم وبين الحج في حق العبد، حتى وجبا عليه، دون الحج؟ قيل: لأن الحج لا يتأتى إلا بالمال غالباً، والعبد لا يملك شيئاً، قال الله تعالى: ﴿عَبْدًا مَمْلُوكًا لَا يَقْدِرُ عَلَى شَيْءٍ . النحل/ ٧٥. ولأن حق المولى في الحج يفوتُ في مدة طويلة، فقدم حق العبد. (۱) مسند الحارث بن أسامة بغية (الحارث) (٤٣٩/١ ، وفيه ضعف، وبدون لفظ: عشر : في غيره أيضاً، ينظر التعريف والإخبار ١٤٥/٢.
His statement: '(upon the free).' He mentioned it in plural form because Hajj is not performed individually but is established by a great assembly, and this is indicated by His statement: 'And due to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House' [Al 'Imran 97]. The condition of freedom is stipulated because the slave is not among its people. The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Any slave who performs Hajj, even ten Hajjs, then becomes free, owes the Hajj of Islam (the obligatory Hajj).' If it is asked: What is the difference between prayer, fasting, and Hajj for a slave, such that the former two are obligatory on him but not Hajj? It is said: Because Hajj generally cannot be performed without wealth, and the slave owns nothing. Allah said: 'A slave who is owned and has no power over anything' [An-Nahl 75]. Also, the master's right over the slave would be lost for a long period during Hajj, so the slave's obligation is waived to give precedence to the master's rights.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage explains the condition of freedom (hurriyah) for the obligation of Hajj. The base text had stated 'upon the free' (على الأحرار), and the commentator elaborates. First, the plural form indicates that Hajj is a communal event requiring a large congregation, not an individual act. Freedom is a condition because the slave is not capable of performing Hajj independently: the slave lacks ownership (milk) required for provisions and expenses, and his master's rights over his service would be suspended for a long period. The proof includes a hadith stating that a slave's previous Hajj does not fulfill the obligatory Hajj after emancipation. A hypothetical objection compares Hajj to prayer and fasting, which are obligatory on slaves despite similar constraints. The answer: prayer and fasting do not require wealth and are shorter in duration, whereas Hajj requires money and prolonged absence. Thus, the slave's obligation is suspended until freedom.

Key Terms
الأحرار (al-aḥrār): Free persons, as opposed to slaves.
العبد (al-ʿabd): A slave who is owned by another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Hajj not obligatory on a slave according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the slave is not a Muslim.
B) Because the slave lacks the necessary wealth and the journey would infringe on the master's rights.
C) Because the slave is not required to perform any acts of worship.
D) Because the hadith exempts slaves explicitly.

Key Takeaway
Freedom is a condition for the obligation of Hajj because the slave lacks ownership and his master's rights would be compromised by the lengthy journey.

The Condition of Freedom for Hajj Obligation
Establishes the condition of freedom for Hajj with proof and addresses a dispute on immediacy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of freedom for Hajj, explain the Hanafi proof, and differentiate between the immediacy and permissibility of delay.

Core Idea
Freedom is a condition for Hajj because the slave lacks wealth and his master's rights take precedence.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar clarifies why Hajj is not obligatory on slaves. It also addresses an internal Hanafi debate about whether the obligation is immediate or can be delayed. You will learn the evidence and the reasoning behind the school's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Condition
Note that the passage begins by stating Hajj is 'upon free persons'. Identify that freedom is a condition for the obligation of Hajj.
The commentator uses the plural 'free persons' because Hajj is performed collectively.
2
Analyze the Proof
Examine the hadith that a slave's Hajj does not fulfill the obligation, and the qiyas (analogy) regarding the slave's lack of ownership and the master's rights.
The proof combines direct hadith (dalil naqli) and rational analogy (dalil aqli).
3
Examine the Objection and Response
Consider why salah and sawm are obligatory on slaves while Hajj is not. Follow the response: because Hajj requires wealth and a prolonged absence.
This distinction is based on the nature of the acts and their requirements.
4
Understand the Dispute on Immediacy
Read the dispute between Muhammad al-Shaybani and Abu Yusuf regarding whether Hajj is immediate (fawr) or can be delayed (tarakhi).
The Prophet's delay is cited as evidence for non-immediacy, but Abu Yusuf argues the Prophet had knowledge of his lifespan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على الأحرار، كتاب الحج وحُجَّةٌ محمد: أن الله تعالى فَرَضَه سنةَ ست، وحج رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سنة عشر ، ولو كان وجوبه على الفور: لم يؤخره. والجواب لأبي يوسف : أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قد علم بطريق الوحي أنه يعيش إلى أن يؤديه، فكان آمنا من فواته. قوله: (على الأحرار). إنما ذكره بلفظ الجمع ؛ لأنه لا يؤدى بمنفرد، بل يُقام بجمع عظيم، وإليه الإشارة بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ . آل عمران / ۹۷ وإنما شرط الحرية؛ لأن العبد ليس من أهله، قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «أيما عبد حج ولو عشر حِجَج ثم أعتق: فعليه حجة الإسلام (۱). فإن قيل: ما الفرق بين الصلاة والصوم وبين الحج في حق العبد، حتى وجبا عليه، دون الحج؟ قيل: لأن الحج لا يتأتى إلا بالمال غالباً، والعبد لا يملك شيئاً، قال الله تعالى: ﴿عَبْدًا مَمْلُوكًا لَا يَقْدِرُ عَلَى شَيْءٍ . النحل/ ٧٥. ولأن حق المولى في الحج يفوتُ في مدة طويلة، فقدم حق العبد على حق الله ؛ لافتقار العبد، وغنى الله بخلاف الصلاة والصوم، فإنهما يتأديان بغير المال، ولا تنقطع خدمة المولى بهما.
(It is obligatory) upon free persons. The Book of Hajj. And the proof of Muhammad (al-Shaybani) is that Allah the Exalted made it obligatory in the year six, and the Messenger of Allah ﷺ performed Hajj in the year ten, and if its obligation was immediate, he would not have delayed it. And the response for Abu Yusuf is that the Prophet ﷺ knew through revelation that he would live to perform it, so he was secure from missing it. His statement: (upon free persons). He mentioned it in the plural form because it is not performed individually, but is established by a great multitude, and to that is the indication of His statement: 'And to Allah is the pilgrimage to the House' [Al 'Imran 97]. And he made freedom a condition because the slave is not from its people. He ﷺ said: 'Any slave who performs Hajj even ten Hajjs and then is freed, upon him is the Hajj of Islam.' If it is said: What is the difference between salah, sawm and Hajj with respect to the slave, such that they are obligatory upon him but not Hajj? It is said: Because Hajj is not accomplished except with wealth generally, and the slave owns nothing, as Allah said: 'a slave owned who has no power over anything' [An-Nahl 75]. And because the right of the master regarding Hajj is lost over a long period, so the right of the slave is given precedence over the right of Allah due to the slave's need, and Allah's self-sufficiency, unlike salah and sawm, for they are performed without wealth, and the service of the master is not interrupted by them.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) of Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar discusses the condition of freedom (hurriyyah) for Hajj. The commentator first addresses an incidental intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad al-Shaybani argues that Hajj obligation is not immediate (fawr) because the Prophet delayed it until year 10, while Abu Yusuf responds that the Prophet knew he would live. This shows the ruling that Hajj can be delayed if one is unable. Then the commentator explains why the author used the plural 'free persons'—Hajj is performed collectively. He then proves the condition of freedom: a slave is not a proper subject for Hajj because he lacks ownership (Quran 16:75) and his master's rights take precedence over a long journey. The objection about why salah and sawm are obligatory on slaves is answered: those acts require no wealth and do not interrupt service. Thus, freedom is a necessary condition for Hajj obligation.

Key Terms
الحج (al-Hajj): The pilgrimage to the House of Allah (Kaaba) in Makkah, an obligatory act once in a lifetime for those who have the means.
الحرية (al-hurriyyah): Freedom; the state of not being a slave. It is a condition for the obligation of Hajj.
الفور (al-fawr): Immediacy; the view that an obligation must be performed as soon as possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because Hajj requires a guide and the slave cannot have a guide.
D) Because the slave is exempt from all acts of worship.

Key Takeaway
Freedom is a condition for Hajj because the slave lacks ownership and his master's rights take precedence over the long journey.

Conditions for Hajj Obligation and the Ruling for the Blind
Explains four conditions for Hajj obligation and an intra-Hanafi dispute on the blind.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for Hajj obligation and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the blind person's duty.

Core Idea
Hajj is wajib on a free, Muslim, adult, sane, and physically able person; the blind person is disputed.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira clarifies the conditions that trigger the obligation of Hajj. The commentator first lists the prerequisites: Islam, adulthood, sanity, and physical health, supported by the hadith of the lifted pen. Then, a key intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two distinguished students (the Sahibayn) is presented: does a blind person with a guide and means become personally obligated? Understanding this difference reveals how the Hanafi school handles cases of permanent versus temporary inability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four conditions
What are the four categories excluded by the text? (Muslims, adults, sane, healthy). Note that each condition is a shart for wajib.
The text uses the phrase 'احترازاً عن' (as a precaution against) to indicate exclusion.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
Which hadith is cited for the exemption of children and the insane? How does it prove the ruling? The hadith 'رفع القلم عن ثلاثة' is a sahih hadith that demonstrates lack of taklif.
This hadith is used to prove that children and insane are not mukallaf, so Hajj is not wajib on them.
3
Understand 'healthy'
What does 'healthy in body and limbs' mean? Which conditions exempt a person? The text mentions the sick, paralyzed, amputee, and chronically ill.
The key is the inability to perform the journey; temporary inability delays obligation, permanent inability substitutes with a proxy.
4
Analyze the dispute on blindness
What is Abu Hanifa's position? (No personal obligation, must send proxy). What is the Sahibayn's position? (Personal obligation if guide and means available).
The dispute hinges on whether blindness is a permanent inability analogous to paralysis or a curable inconvenience.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? If a blind person performs Hajj personally, Abu Hanifa says it is valid but not obligatory; Sahibayn say it is obligatory and proxy invalid.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
* قوله: (المسلمين (۱) ، البالغين) احترازاً عن الصبيان؛ لأن العبادات موضوعةٌ عنهم؛ لأنهم غير مكلفين. * قوله : (العقلاء): يحترز عن المجانين قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: رفع القلم عن ثلاثة : عن الصبي حتى يحتلم، وعن المجنون حتى يفيق، وعن النائم حتى يستيقظ » (٢). قوله : (الأصحاء) : أي أصحاء البدن والجوارح، حتى لا يجب على المريض والمقعد ومقطوع اليد والرجل ، والزَّمِن؛ لأن العجز عن العبادة يؤثر في سقوطها ما دام العجز باقياً. - واختلفوا في الأعمى : فعند أبي حنيفة : لا حج عليه وإن وجد قائداً، ويجب في ماله. وعندهما: يجب عليه إذا وجد قائداً وزاداً، وراحلة، ومن يكفيه مؤنة سَفره في خدمته، ولا يجزئه أن يحج عنه غيره.
His statement: (Muslims, adults) as a precaution against children, because acts of worship are not obligated upon them because they are not legally responsible. His statement: (sane) as a precaution against the insane. He ﷺ said: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the child until he reaches puberty, from the insane until he recovers, and from the sleeping until he awakens.' His statement: (healthy) meaning healthy in body and limbs, such that it is not obligatory upon the sick, the paralyzed, the one with cut hand and foot, and the chronically ill, because inability to perform worship affects its obligation as long as the inability remains. - And they differed regarding the blind: According to Abu Hanifa, Hajj is not obligatory upon him even if he finds a guide, and it is obligatory in his wealth (i.e., he must send someone else). According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is obligatory upon him if he finds a guide, provision, a mount, and someone who suffices for the expenses of his travel in his service, and it is not permissible for someone else to perform Hajj on his behalf.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the conditions for Hajj obligation. The author first explains that 'Muslims and adults' excludes children, as they are not mukallaf (legally responsible). The hadith of the lifted pen confirms that children and the insane are exempt from obligations. Next, 'sane' excludes the insane. Then 'healthy' refers to physical soundness; those with chronic illnesses or disabilities that prevent travel are exempt as long as the inability lasts. The key dispute concerns the blind: Abu Hanifa holds that Hajj is never obligatory on a blind person even if he has a guide, because blindness is considered a permanent disability that prevents safe travel. Instead, the blind person must pay someone else to perform Hajj on his behalf (Hajj badal). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that if the blind person can find a guide, provision, and a mount, and someone to handle travel expenses, then Hajj becomes obligatory on him personally, and it is not valid for him to send a proxy. This difference stems from whether blindness is analogous to a curable or incurable condition. Abu Hanifa considers it like a permanent inability, while the Sahibayn see it as an inconvenience that can be overcome with assistance.

Key Terms
البالغون (al-balighun): Adults who have reached puberty; condition for Hajj obligation.
العقلاء (al-ʿuqala'): Sane persons; those who are not insane.
الأصحاء (al-asihha'): Healthy in body and limbs; excluding those with chronic illness or disability preventing travel.
الأعمى (al-aʿma): A blind person; subject to ikhtilaf among Hanafi imams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a blind person who has a guide and sufficient provisions?
A) He is obligated to perform Hajj personally according to all Hanafi imams
B) He is not obligated at all and need not send a proxy
C) According to Abu Hanifa, he is not obligated personally and must send a proxy; according to the Sahibayn, he is obligated personally
D) He is obligated to perform Hajj only if he can find a mount

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi view on the blind is that personal obligation is lifted; they must send a proxy.

Conditions for Hajj Obligation: Islam, Adulthood, Sanity, Health & the Case of the Blind
States conditions for Hajj obligation and discusses blind and ill

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for Hajj obligation and explain the Hanafi differences regarding the blind person's obligation.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory only on the Muslim, adult, sane, and healthy – the blind are exempt according to Abu Hanifa, but obliged by the Sahibayn if aided.

Hajj is one of the five pillars, but its obligation is contingent on specific conditions. In this passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayra, the commentator Sharif al-Jurjani clarifies the four conditions from the matn of Al-Quduri: Muslim, adult, sane, and healthy. He then delves into a significant intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the blind person, which hinges on the interpretation of 'health' and the ability to perform the rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that Hajj is being ruled upon, and identify the level of obligation (fard 'ayn) and the conditions that trigger it.
The text begins 'كتاب الحج' and immediately lists the conditions.
2
List the four conditions from the text
Extract the four conditions: being Muslim, adult (baligh), sane ('aqil), and healthy (sound in body and limbs). Understand each as a necessary condition for obligation.
The Arabic terms: المسلمين، البالغين، العقلاء، الأصحاء.
3
Understand the proof for exemption of child and insane
The commentator cites the hadith 'رفع القلم عن ثلاثة' to prove that children and the insane are not obligated. Identify this as dalil naqli (textual evidence) and note its status as zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi debate on the blind
The text presents a difference between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn) on whether a blind person who has a guide, provisions, and a mount is obligated for Hajj. State each position clearly and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
Abu Hanifa: no obligation on the person, but must send someone from his wealth. Sahibayn: obligated if he has the means.
5
Apply the ruling to illness
The text distinguishes between illness hoped for recovery (obligation deferred until recovery) and permanent inability (obligation drops). Relate this to the condition of health.
If the illness is temporary, he must perform Hajj himself after recovery; another cannot do it on his behalf.

The Book of Hajj. (Page 319) Muslims, adults, sane, healthy. Obligation due to the right of Allah; because of the poverty of the servant and the self-sufficiency of Allah, contrary to prayer and fasting, for they are performed without wealth, and the service of the Master is not discontinued by them. * His saying: (Muslims, adults) is a caution against children because acts of worship are not required of them, as they are not legally responsible. * His saying: (sane) is a caution against the insane; the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The pen has been lifted from three: from the child until he reaches puberty, from the insane until he regains sanity, and from the sleeper until he wakes up.' (2) His saying: (healthy) means sound in body and limbs, so that it is not obligatory on the sick, the paralyzed, the one with amputated hand or foot, and the chronically ill; because inability for worship affects its annulment as long as the inability remains. - They differed concerning the blind: According to Abu Hanifa: Hajj is not obligatory on him even if he finds a guide, and it is obligatory from his wealth. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): it is obligatory on him if he finds a guide, provisions, a mount, and someone to suffice him the expenses of his travel in his service, and it is not sufficient for someone else to perform Hajj on his behalf. (1) The word 'Muslims' is established in the copy of al-Quduri 745 AH, 1309 AH, and see al-Ikhtiyar 1/140. (2) Sunan Abi Dawud (4398), Sunan al-Nasa'i 6/156, Sunan Ibn Majah (2041), and authenticated by Ibn al-Mulaqqin in al-Badr al-Munir 6/148. As for inability due to illness if it is an illness hoped to be removed: Hajj becomes obligatory after its removal, and the Hajj of someone else is not sufficient for him, and he is obliged to perform Hajj himself after recovery.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayra, a commentary on al-Mukhtasar al-Quduri, begins the Book of Hajj by enumerating the conditions for the obligation of Hajj. The text specifies four conditions: being Muslim, adult, sane, and healthy. It explains that 'Muslim' excludes non-Muslims, 'adult' excludes children (as they are not legally responsible—mukallaf), and 'sane' excludes the insane, citing the hadith 'the pen is lifted from three' (child, insane, sleeper). 'Healthy' excludes those with physical incapacity such as the sick, paralyzed, amputated, or chronically ill, since inability to perform the acts of worship leads to their non-obligation as long as the inability persists. The passage then addresses a difference of opinion regarding the blind person. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, Hajj is not obligatory on the blind even if he has a guide; rather, it is obligatory on his wealth (meaning he should send someone else on his behalf). According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), Hajj is obligatory on the blind person if he has a guide, provisions, a mount, and someone to serve him during the journey; in that case, it is not valid for another to perform Hajj on his behalf. Finally, the passage discusses inability due to illness: if the illness is one from which recovery is expected, Hajj becomes obligatory after recovery, and it is not sufficient for someone else to perform it on his behalf; he must perform it himself once cured.

Key Terms
مكلف (mukallaf): Legally responsible person; one who is Muslim, adult, sane.
الأعمى (al-a'mā): The blind person.
الزَّمِن (al-zamin): Chronically ill person with permanent disability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The child, the insane, and the sleeper.
B) The child, the insane, and the drunk.
C) The child, the elderly, and the sick.
D) The insane, the blind, and the sick.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is obligatory on the Muslim, adult, sane, and healthy, but the blind are subject to a valid internal Hanafi disagreement on whether they must perform it themselves or send a proxy.

Condition of Istita'ah: Provisions and Mount, and Preferred Mode of Travel
Explains the condition of having provisions and mount by ownership, and discusses walking vs riding preference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement of ownership for provisions and mount for Hajj, and distinguish between the two Hanafi narrations on the preference of walking versus riding.

Core Idea
Ownership of provisions and mount is required for Hajj; the ruling on walking vs riding is unresolved but walking has stronger textual support.

This lesson continues the commentary on the condition of istita'ah (ability) for Hajj. The text clarifies that 'provisions and mount' must be owned, not borrowed. It also addresses a secondary question: is it better to walk or ride? Two narrations from Abu Hanifa are presented, leaving the matter open.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on istita'ah
The passage rules that Hajj becomes obligatory only when one owns provisions and a mount. This is not just having them available, but owning them.
Ownership (milk) is explicitly required.
2
Identify the condition of ownership
The text specifies that 'power over provisions and mount' means ownership, not mere permission (ibaha) or borrowing (ariya). Even if permission comes from someone with no favor (minna), it does not suffice.
3
Note the distance exemption for mount
The mount is only required if the distance to Makkah is three days or more. For shorter distances, walking suffices if the person is able.
4
Trace the proof for the preference of walking
The Quranic verse (22:27) mentions 'on foot' first, indicating precedence. The hadith promises multiplied rewards for each step of a walking pilgrim.
The hadith is cited as evidence for walking's merit.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on walking vs riding
Two narrations from Abu Hanifa are reported: one via al-Hasan says riding is better (to avoid spoiling character), another says walking is better (with textual proofs). The author does not give tarjih.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.

His saying: (When they have power over provisions and a mount). Meaning by way of ownership, not by way of permission and borrowing, whether the permission is from someone who has no favor over him like parents and children, or from others. And the mount is only required for the one between him and Makkah three days or more. As for less than that: it is not required if he is able to walk. But it is necessary that they have enough food for themselves and their dependents in a proper manner until their return. If it is said: What is better, to perform Hajj walking or riding? It is said: Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that performing Hajj riding is better because walking spoils one's character. And it is narrated that performing Hajj walking is better because Allah the Exalted gave precedence to walkers; He said: 'They will come to you on foot and on every lean camel' (al-Hajj 27). And in the hadith: 'Whoever performs Hajj walking, Allah writes for him for every step a good deed of the Haram. It was said: O Messenger of Allah, what are the good deeds of the Haram? He said: one is multiplied seven hundred times.' (1)
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the condition of istita'ah (ability) for Hajj. The text explains that 'power over provisions and mount' means ownership (milk), not mere permission (ibaha) or borrowing ('ariya), even if the permission is from someone like parents who generally have no favor (minna) over the person. The mount is required only for those who are three days' travel or more from Makkah; for shorter distances, walking suffices if the person is able. Additionally, sufficient food must be available for the pilgrim and his dependents until his return. The passage then addresses a question of preference (afdaliyya): Is it better to perform Hajj walking or riding? Two narrations are reported from Abu Hanifa: one (via al-Hasan) states that riding is better because walking may spoil one's character (khuluq); another narration states that walking is better, citing the Quranic verse 'They will come to you on foot and on every lean camel' (22:27) which mentions walkers first, and a hadith promising immense rewards for each step. The text does not definitively choose one view, leaving the matter of preference open.

Key Terms
الزاد والراحلة (al-zād wa al-rāḥilah): Provisions (food) and mount (riding animal) necessary for travel to Hajj.
المنة (al-minnah): Favor or obligation; the text says 'no favor on him' meaning the lender (like parents) does not confer a favor that would make acceptance problematic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The mount is not required if he can walk.
C) The mount is required only if he is sick.
D) The mount can be borrowed.

Key Takeaway
Ownership of provisions and mount is the Hanafi condition for Hajj obligation; the preference between walking and riding remains an unresolved ikhtilaf within the madhhab.

Conditions of Istita'ah for Hajj: Ownership of Provisions and Mount
Explaining conditions of istita'ah for Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions of istita'ah for Hajj according to the Hanafi school, explain the requirement of ownership (milk) rather than permission, and identify the distance threshold for requiring a mount.

Core Idea
Ownership of provisions and a mount, plus surplus over basic needs, is required for Hajj to be obligatory.

The obligation of Hajj hinges on istita'ah (ability). But what exactly constitutes ability? This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira clarifies that ability means ownership of provisions and a mount, not mere permission. It also discusses the nuance of walking vs. riding and the requirement of surplus beyond basic needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions
Identify the three key elements that must be possessed for Hajj to become fard according to the passage: ownership of provisions (zad), ownership of a mount (rahilah) for distances of three days or more, and surplus (fadlan) over basic needs.
These are not the pillars of Hajj but conditions for its obligation.
2
Analyze the ownership requirement
Examine why the text emphasizes milk (ownership) over ibaha (permission). Note that even if provisions are given freely (e.g., by parents), if ownership is not transferred, Hajj is not obligatory.
Ownership means full control over the resources.
3
Determine the distance threshold
Understand that the mount is required only for those whose journey to Mecca is three days or more. For shorter distances, walking suffices if one is able.
The three-day threshold is based on the customary travel distance in early Islam.
4
Resolve the walking vs. riding debate
Consider the two transmitted positions from Abu Hanifa: one holds riding is better to avoid hardship, another holds walking is better based on Quran and hadith. Note that neither view changes the obligation; walking is virtuous but not required.
For a vow to walk, al-Hidayah requires not riding until tawaf al-ziyarah, while al-Asl gives a choice.

Book of Hajj. If they have the means for provisions and a mount... As for inability due to illness that is hoped to be cured: Hajj becomes obligatory upon him after recovery, and the Hajj of another does not suffice for him, and he must perform Hajj himself after cure. And it is narrated that al-Hasan ibn Ali, may Allah be pleased with them both, used to walk in his Hajj while his riding animals were led beside him. He said in al-Hidayah: Whoever imposes upon himself to perform Hajj walking, he should not ride until he performs tawaf al-ziyarah. And in al-Asl: he is given a choice between riding and walking. In the first there is an indication of obligation because he committed to an act of worship in its complete form, so it becomes binding in that form, like if he vows to fast consecutively. If he rides, he spills blood (offers a sacrifice) because he introduced a deficiency. His statement: (surplus) is in the accusative as a hal from provisions and the mount. Commentary
This passage addresses the conditions that must be met for Hajj to become obligatory (fard). It begins by clarifying that the ability (istita'ah) referred to in the verse requires ownership (milk) of provisions and a mount, not mere permission or borrowing. The mount is only required for those whose distance to Mecca is three days or more; for shorter distances, walking suffices if one is able. Additionally, one must have sufficient provisions for himself and his family until his return. The text then discusses the preference between walking and riding. There are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one that riding is better because walking may harm one's character, and another that walking is better, supported by Quran and hadith. The author cites Ibn Abbas' regret and al-Hasan ibn Ali's practice. The issue of a vow to walk is also addressed: according to al-Hidayah, if one vows to walk, he must not ride until after tawaf al-ziyarah; if he does ride, he must offer a sacrifice. According to al-Asl, he has a choice. Finally, the requirement of surplus (fadlan) over basic needs like dwelling, servant, and furniture is mentioned, which is a condition for istita'ah.

Key Terms
الزاد (al-zad): Provisions necessary for the journey, such as food and drink.
الراحلة (al-rahilah): A mount (camel, horse, etc.) sufficient for travel, required if distance is three days or more.
الملك (al-milk): Ownership of the provisions and mount, not mere permission or loan.
فاضلاً (fadilan): Surplus over basic needs such as dwelling, servant, furniture, and clothing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Hajj becomes obligatory only when one owns provisions and a mount (if distance ≥3 days), and has surplus beyond basic needs for self and family.

Conditions for Hajj Obligation and the Vow to Walk
Commentary expanding on conditions for Hajj and a vow-to-walk case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for Hajj obligation (surplus wealth, family maintenance, safe route, mahram), distinguish safety as a condition of performance versus obligation, and apply the qiyas on a vow to walk to determine the ruling.

Core Idea
Hajj requires surplus wealth, safe route as performance condition, and mahram for women; a vow to walk is binding until tawaf al-ziyarah, riding requires dam.

This commentary from al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah expands on the conditions in Mukhtasar al-Quduri for Hajj obligation. It also addresses a person who vows to walk for Hajj, clarifying the ruling through qiyas. Understanding these conditions is essential for determining when Hajj is fard and how related vows are fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Hajj is fard 'ayn once in a lifetime when the conditions of istita'ah (capacity) are met. The passage expands on these conditions from the matn.
The ruling level is fard, established by Quran and Sunnah.
2
List the conditions of obligation
From the text: surplus wealth beyond residence and indispensable items (including debts), moderate maintenance for family and servants for the journey and return, safety of the route (as condition of performance, not obligation), and for women a mahram or husband.
Abu Yusuf requires surplus for one month after return, but some mashayikh do not require that.
3
Analyze the dispute on safety of route
Some scholars treat safety as a condition of obligation (no bequest if dies), but the preferred view (al-Nihayah) treats it as a condition of performance (postpone, but bequest if dies).
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether the dying person must bequeath for Hajj.
4
Examine the vow to walk
If someone vows to perform Hajj walking, al-Hidayah holds it binding to walk until Tawaf al-Ziyarah; al-Asl gives choice. The preferred view imposes obligation because the vow specified an attribute of perfection (sifat al-kamal).
If the person rides, he must offer a dam (sacrifice) as compensation for deficiency.
5
Apply the principle of qiyas
The vow to walk is analogized (qiyas) to a vow of consecutive fasting. In both cases, the person committed to an act with a specific perfection; breaking that attribute requires compensation (dam for Hajj, qada+kaffarah for fasting).
The illa is undertaking worship with a specific attribute of perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
فاضلاً عن مسكنه، وما لا بد منه، وعن ابن عباس أنه قال بعد ما كف بصره : ما تأسفتُ على شيء: كتابسي على أن أحج ماشياً (١). وروي «أن الحسن بن علي رضي الله عنهما كان يمشي في حجه، والجنائب (٢) تقاد إلى جنبه (٣). قال في الهداية (4) : ومَن جعل على نفسه أن يحج ماشياً: فإنه لا يركب حتى يطوف طواف الزيارة. وفي «الأصل»: خيره بين الركوب والمشي. ففي الأول إشارة إلى الوجوب ؛ لأنه التزم القُربة بصفة الكمال: فلزمه بتلك الصفة، كما إذا نذر الصوم متتابعاً، فإن ركب : أراق دماً؛ لأنه أدخل نقصاً فيه. قوله : ( فاضلاً) : انتصب على الحال من الزاد والراحلة.

Book of Hajj. ... surplus beyond his residence and what is indispensable, and from Ibn Abbas that he said after his sight was lost: I never regretted anything like my regret for not performing Hajj walking. And it is narrated that al-Hasan ibn Ali (may Allah be pleased with them both) used to walk in his Hajj while the led horses were being led beside him. Al-Hidayah said: Whoever imposes upon himself to perform Hajj walking: he may not ride until he performs the tawaf of visitation. And in al-Asl: he is given choice between riding and walking. In the first there is an indication of obligation because he undertook the act of worship with the attribute of perfection: so it becomes binding with that attribute, just as if he vows to fast consecutively, then if he rides he spills blood (offers sacrifice) because he introduced a deficiency. His saying: (surplus) is in the accusative case as a circumstantial qualifier from provision and mount. * His saying: (beyond his residence and what is indispensable such as the servant, furniture, clothes, his horse, his weapon, and repayment of his debts. And it is said: surplus beyond the dowers of women. And it is said: that is not required.) * His saying: (and for the maintenance of his family until the time of his return) meaning moderate maintenance, neither extravagant nor stingy. And similarly for the maintenance of his servants. And from Abu Yusuf: it should be surplus for one month after his return because he cannot earn due to weakness from travel. And some of our shaykhs do not consider that. As in al-Wajiz. * His saying: (and the route was safe) meaning at the time of departure of the people of his town. And they differed whether safety of the route is a condition of obligation or a condition of performance? Some said: from the conditions of obligation, such that if he dies before it is not obligatory to enjoin it. He does not perform Hajj. And it was said: from the conditions of performance, such that if he dies before performing Hajj, he must enjoin it. Al-Nihayah said: that is correct. * His saying: (And for the woman it is considered that she have a mahram to perform Hajj with her, or a husband.) And this hadith is authentic in chain, but they did not record it. End. Al-Dhahabi said in Talkhis al-Mustadrak: it is not authentic, I fear it is a lie, and Isa narrated it; Abu Hatim said: he is denounced in hadith. End. And al-Nawawi weakened it in al-Majmu' 7/92. Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh of al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah expands on the conditions for Hajj obligation as stated in Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The commentator first explains the condition of having surplus wealth beyond one's residence and basic necessities, including servant, furniture, clothes, horse, weapon, and debts. He mentions a difference of opinion regarding whether surplus for dowers (sadaq) is required. Then he discusses the maintenance of family and servants during the journey, and a view from Abu Yusuf that surplus for a month after return is needed. The condition of a safe route is examined: is it a condition for obligation or for performance? The preferred view (from al-Nihayah) is that it is a condition for performance, meaning if the route becomes unsafe, one must wait, but if one dies before performing Hajj, he should bequeath it. Finally, for women, a mahram (unmarriageable kin) or husband is required. The passage also includes a digression on a vow to walk to Hajj, citing al-Hidayah and al-Asl. The principle: if one vows to perform an act of worship with a specific perfection (like walking in Hajj), it becomes binding as such; riding would require a dam (sacrifice) as compensation, analogous to a vow of consecutive fasting. The footnotes discuss the authenticity of the hadith about Ibn Abbas and al-Hasan.

Key Terms
فاضلاً (fādilan): Surplus wealth beyond one's essential needs (residence, basic necessities, debts, etc.)
مَحْرَم (maḥram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently forbidden, such as father, brother, son, etc.
نفقة وسط (nafaqah wasaṭ): Moderate maintenance for family and servants, neither extravagant nor stingy.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal required as compensation for certain violations or incomplete fulfillments in Hajj or vows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the Hanafi school, is the safety of the route a condition for the obligation of Hajj or for its performance?
A) A condition for obligation – if the route is unsafe, Hajj is not wajib at all.
B) A condition for performance – if unsafe, one delays but must still intend and bequeath if death approaches.
C) Not a condition at all – one must go even if unsafe.
D) Only for women is it a condition, not for men.

Key Takeaway
The conditions for Hajj obligation include surplus wealth, moderate maintenance, safe route (as performance condition), and mahram for women; a vow to walk is binding, with dam required for riding.

Provision for Dependents: A Condition for Hajj
Commentary on condition of provision for dependents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of having provision for dependents for Hajj and explain the Hanafi dispute regarding a surplus after return.

Core Idea
Provision for dependents must be moderate, covering the journey and return; a month's extra surplus is recommended but not obligatory.

We now examine a key condition for Hajj being obligatory: the pilgrim must have enough provision for their dependents during their absence. This commentary clarifies that the provision should be moderate – not wasteful nor stingy – and includes both family and servants. A subtle intra-Hanafi difference emerges: does one also need a month's surplus after returning?

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is the condition of istita'a (capability) for Hajj. The specific condition is having provision (nafaqa) for one's dependents. This is a prerequisite for Hajj to become obligatory (fard).
Without this provision, Hajj is not obligatory.
2
Understand 'moderate provision'
The text says 'نفقة وسط' – moderate provision, meaning neither extravagant (israf) nor miserly (taqtir). It is the average amount sufficient for the family and servants during the entire journey and return.
This avoids burdening the pilgrim excessively.
3
Note Abu Yusuf's additional condition
Abu Yusuf (rahimahullah) holds that one should also have surplus for one month after returning, because after a long journey one may be too weak to earn immediately. This is an ihtiyati (precautionary) view.
It is based on concern for the traveler's post-journey state.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that moderate provision for the journey and return is sufficient; the month's extra surplus is not obligatory. This is the view of most mashayikh (later scholars) and is found in al-Wajiz and al-Hidayah.
The month surplus is a recommended precaution, not a condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
* قوله: (وعن نفقة عياله إلى حين عوده)، يعني نفقة وسط، لا نفقة إسراف ولا تقتير.
وكذا عن نفقة خدمه.
وعن أبي يوسف: ينبغي أن يكون فاضلاً نفقة عن شهر بعد رجوعه ; لأنه لا يقدر على الكسب ; باعتبار الضعف في السفر.
ومن مشايخنا من لا يعتبر ذلك. كذا في «الوجيز».
His saying: (And about the maintenance of his family until the time of his return) meaning moderate maintenance, neither extravagant nor miserly. Likewise, the maintenance of his servants. And from Abu Yusuf: It should be surplus for a month after his return, because he cannot earn due to weakness in travel. And among our mashayikh are those who do not consider that. As in al-Wajiz.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the condition of istita'a (capability) for Hajj regarding provision for one's dependents. The commentator explains the matn: the required maintenance is moderate (wasat) – not excessive (israf) nor stingy (taqtir). This includes both family and servants. Abu Yusuf adds that the provision should be enough for a month after returning because the traveler may be too weak to earn immediately. However, some later scholars (mashayikh) do not require this surplus. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that moderate provision for the duration of travel and return is sufficient; the extra month is an additional precaution but not obligatory.

Key Terms
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance or provision for one's dependents, including food, clothing, and shelter.
وسط (wasat): Moderate, middle, neither excessive nor deficient.
عيال (iyal): Dependents, including family members and servants whom one is obliged to support.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Minimal subsistence
B) Moderate, neither extravagant nor stingy
C) Double the usual amount
D) The richest possible provision

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position: provision for dependents during Hajj must be moderate and cover the journey and return; the month surplus is a precaution, not a condition.

Road Safety: Condition of Obligation or Performance?
Dispute on whether road safety is shart al-wujub or shart al-ada'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shart al-wujub and shart al-ada' in the Hanafi school and apply the distinction to the case of road safety for Hajj, including the obligation to make a will.

Core Idea
Road safety is a condition of performance, not obligation — Hajj becomes due but you may delay it until safe.

This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah presents an internal Hanafi debate regarding the role of road safety (amn al-tariq) in the obligation of Hajj. The dispute centres on whether safety is a condition for Hajj to be obligatory at all (shart al-wujub) or a condition for its valid performance (shart al-ada'). Understanding this distinction has practical consequences for making a will (isa') if one dies before performing.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the core question: is road safety a condition for the obligation to perform Hajj (shart al-wujub) or a condition for its valid performance (shart al-ada')?
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; both views are from Hanafi scholars.
2
Identify the first view (shart al-wujub)
Some Hanafis hold that if the road is unsafe, Hajj is not obligatory at all. Consequently, if one dies without performing Hajj, no will (isa') is required.
This view absolves the person of any liability.
3
Identify the second view (shart al-ada')
Other Hanafis hold that Hajj remains obligatory, but the unsafe road is an excuse for delaying performance. However, if one dies before performing, a will must be made for someone else to perform it on their behalf.
This is the preferred view in al-Nihayah.
4
Note the tarjih
The author of al-Nihayah declares the second view (shart al-ada') as correct (al-sahih). This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school.
Tarjih is based on textual evidence and ijtihad, though not specified in this passage.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a person living in a town surrounded by bandits. If they die before performing Hajj, according to the mufta bihi, they must have made a will for Hajj to be performed on their behalf.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether a will is obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
* قوله : (وكان الطريق آمناً)، يعني وقت خروج أهل بلده.
- واختلفوا في أمن الطريق هل هو من شرائط الوجوب، أو من شرائط الأداء؟
قال بعضهم : من شرائط الوجوب، حتى إنه إذا مات قبل أن يجب عليه الإيصاء به.
يحج : لا
وقيل: من شرائط الأداء، حتى إنه إذا مات قبل أن يحج: يجب عليه الإيصاء به. قال في «النهاية»: وهو الصحيح.
His saying: (And the road was safe), meaning at the time of the departure of the people of his town. And they differed regarding the safety of the road: is it a condition of obligation or a condition of performance? Some said: it is a condition of obligation, such that if he dies before it becomes obligatory, he does not have to make a will regarding it. And it was said: it is a condition of performance, such that if he dies before performing Hajj, he must make a will regarding it. In al-Nihayah, it is said: this is correct.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the safety of the road is a condition for Hajj being obligatory (shart al-wujub) or a condition for valid performance (shart al-ada'). If it is a condition of obligation, then if the road is unsafe, Hajj is not obligatory, and one does not need to make a will (isaa') for someone else to perform it on their behalf if they die. If it is a condition of performance, then Hajj is obligatory in principle, but the unsafe road excuses immediate performance; however, if one dies without performing, they must make a will for it. The commentator states that the correct view (as in al-Nihayah) is that it is a condition of performance, meaning the obligation remains and one must arrange for it posthumously if prevented.

Key Terms
أمن الطريق (amn al-tariq): Safety of the travel route from dangers such as bandits or wild animals.
الإيصاء (al-isa'): Making a will or commissioning someone to perform Hajj on one's behalf.
شرط الوجوب (shart al-wujub): A condition that must exist for the obligation to arise; if absent, the act is not required.
شرط الأداء (shart al-ada'): A condition that must exist for valid performance; if absent, the obligation remains but performance is delayed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in al-Nihayah, what happens if a person dies before performing Hajj due to an unsafe road?
A) No obligation existed, so no will is needed
B) They must make a will for someone to perform Hajj on their behalf
C) Their heirs must perform Hajj for them
D) The obligation is waived entirely

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that road safety is a condition of performance; thus, Hajj remains obligatory and a will must be made if one dies before performing.
