Prohibitions for the Muhrim in Ihram
Commentary on prohibitions for the pilgrim in ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key prohibitions for a muhrim in ihram according to the Hanafi school and identify the dalil (proof) for each prohibition, distinguishing between haram and makruh actions.

Core Idea
The muhrim avoids direct perfume, head/face covering, shaving, and dyed clothes; carrying loads or wearing a perfumed garment is allowed.

In this passage, the commentator expands on the matn of al-Quduri regarding what a pilgrim in ihram must avoid. The rulings are derived from the Quran and Sunnah, with careful distinctions between direct and indirect acts. Understanding these prohibitions is essential for a valid Hajj or Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
List each prohibited act mentioned: covering head/face, applying perfume, shaving, trimming beard/nails, wearing dyed clothes. Note that some acts are haram (e.g., applying perfume) while others are makruh (e.g., smelling perfume).
The commentator clarifies that carrying a load on the head is not covering.
2
Locate the dalil
For shaving, the verse from al-Baqarah 2:196 is cited. For wearing red clothes, a hadith is quoted, though its chain is weak.
Also note the logical analogy: trimming beard/nails is like shaving.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic imperative 'do not shave' indicates prohibition (nahy). The hadith's explicit forbiddance of red implies it is haram for the muhrim.
Weak chain reduces the ruling to makruh for non-muhrim men, but for muhrim it remains prohibited.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school permits men to cover the face in ihram, while Hanafis prohibit it. The text does not discuss this, but it is a known difference.
Also, all schools agree on the prohibition of shaving except for necessity.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is as stated: these prohibitions are established in the zahir al-riwayah, and the mufta bihi is that they are haram with exceptions for necessity requiring dam.
The weak hadith on red clothes does not affect the ruling for muhrim, as other proofs exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
ولا يُغطي رأسه، ولا وجهه . ولا يَمَسُّ طِيْباً .
ولا يحلق رأسه، ولا شعرَ بدنه،
والكعب هنا : هو الناتئ في وسط القدم عند معقد الشراك. قوله: (ولا يُغطي رأسه، ولا وجهه)، يعني التغطية المعهودة. أما لو حَمَل على رأسه عدل بُر، وشبهه : فلا شيء عليه؛ لأن ذلك لا يحصل به المقصود من الارتفاق.
قوله: (ولا يمس طيباً)، وكذا لا يدَّهنُ.
ولا بأس أن يلبس الثوب المبخّرَ ؛ لأنه غير مستعمل لجزء من الطيب، وإنما يحصل له مجرد الرائحة، وذلك لا يكون تطيباً. ويكره له شم الريحان، والطيب، وليس عليه في ذلك شيء؛ لأنه غير مستعمل لجزء منه.
ولا بأس أن يكتحل إذا لم يكن الكحل مطيباً. ولا بأس أن يحتجم ، ويفتصد، ويُجبر الكسر. وليس له أن يختضب بالحناء؛ لأنه طيب.
ويكره له أن يقبل امرأته أو يضاجعها.
* قوله: (ولا يحلق رأسه، ولا شعرَ بدنه ؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُءُوسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الهَدَى يَحِلَّهُ . البقرة / ١٩٦ : أي حتى يبلغ الهدي الحرم،
ويعلم أن هديه قد ذُبح في الحرم.
ويستوي في ذلك الحلقُ بالموسى ، والنُّورة، والنتف، والقلع بالأسنان. * قوله : (ولا يقص من لحيته، ولا من ظُفُره)؛ لأنه في معنى الحلق، ولأن فيه إزالة الشعث، وقضاءَ التَّفَث.
قال في «الكرخي»: قضاء التفث هو: قص الشعر، وحلق الرأس، وتقليم الأظفار، ونتف الإبط، وحلق العانة.
وقيل: : التفث : الوسخ من طول الشعر والأظفار، وقضاؤه: إزالته.
قوله: (ولا يلبس ثوباً مصبوغاً ،بورس، ولا بزعفران، ولا بعصفر).
ولا ينبغي له أن يتوسده، ولا ينام عليه.
وهل يكره لبسه لغير المحرم من الرجال؟
روي قال : أن ابن عمر نهاني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن لبس الحُمْرة، وقال: إياكم والحمرة، فإنها زي الشيطان»(۱).
(1) معجم الطبراني الكبير ١٤٨/١٨ ، قال الهيثمي في مجمع الزوائد ١٣٠/٥ : رواه الطبراني بإسنادين في أحدهما : يعقوب بن خالد بن نجيح البكري العبدي، ولم أعرفه، وفي الآخر: بكر بن محمد يروي عن سعيد عن شعبة، وبقية رجالهما ثقات، ورواه في الأوسط، وفيه أبو بكر الهذلي، وهو ضعيف. اهـ، وقال العلامة
Book of Hajj. And he does not cover his head, nor his face. And he does not touch perfume. And he does not shave his head, nor any hair of his body. And the ankle here: it is the protrusion in the middle of the foot at the knot of the shoelace. His saying: (And he does not cover his head, nor his face) means the usual covering. But if he carries on his head a load of wheat and the like, there is nothing upon him; because the purpose of comfort is not achieved by that. His saying: (And he does not touch perfume), and likewise he does not apply oil. There is no harm in his wearing a perfumed garment; because it is not used with a part of the perfume, only the mere scent reaches him, and that is not perfuming. And it is disliked for him to smell basil and perfume, and there is nothing upon him in that; because he is not using a part of it. There is no harm in his applying kohl if the kohl is not perfumed. There is no harm in his undergoing cupping, bloodletting, and setting a fracture. And he may not dye with henna; because it is perfume. And it is disliked for him to kiss his wife or lie beside her. * His saying: (And he does not shave his head, nor any hair of his body) due to His statement, Exalted: 'And do not shave your heads until the sacrificial animal reaches its place of slaughter.' (al-Baqarah 2:196) i.e., until the sacrificial animal reaches the sanctuary, and he knows that his offering has been slaughtered in the sanctuary. And in that regard, shaving with a razor, depilatory cream, plucking, and pulling by teeth are equal. * His saying: (And he does not trim his beard, nor his nail) because it is similar to shaving, and because it involves removing dishevelment and performing tafath. He said in 'al-Karkhi': The performance of tafath is: cutting hair, shaving the head, trimming nails, plucking armpit hair, and shaving pubic hair. And it is said: al-tafath is the dirt from length of hair and nails, and its performance is its removal. His saying: (And he does not wear a garment dyed with wars, nor with saffron, nor with safflower). And he should not use it as a pillow, nor sleep on it. And is it disliked for him to wear it for a non-muhrim among men? It is narrated that Ibn 'Umar said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade me from wearing red, and said: 'Beware of red, for it is the dress of the devil.' (1) (1) Mu'jam al-Tabarani al-Kabir 148/18; al-Haythami said in Majma' al-Zawa'id 130/5: It was narrated by al-Tabarani with two chains: in one of them is Ya'qub ibn Khalid ibn Najih al-Bakri al-'Abdi, and I do not know him; in the other is Bakr ibn Muhammad narrating from Sa'id from Shu'bah, and the rest of their narrators are trustworthy; and it is narrated in al-Awsat with Abu Bakr al-Hudhali, who is weak. And al-'Allamah said...
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This is a commentary expanding on the matn of al-Quduri regarding prohibitions for the muhrim (pilgrim in ihram). The commentator explains each ruling with clarifications and exceptions. The passage begins with a definition of the ankle (ka'b) from the previous section on wudu, which may be a scanning artifact. The main rulings: the muhrim must not cover his head or face in the usual manner; carrying a load on the head is permissible as it does not constitute covering. Touching perfume is prohibited, and by extension applying oil. However, wearing a garment that has been perfumed (e.g., by incense) is permissible because the scent is not from direct application. Smelling basil or perfume is merely disliked (makruh), not prohibited, as no physical part of the perfume is used. Applying non-perfumed kohl, cupping, and setting fractures are allowed. Dyeing with henna is prohibited as it is considered perfume. Kissing or lying beside one's spouse is disliked. Shaving the head or any body hair is prohibited, even by plucking or using depilatory cream, based on the Quranic verse (2:196). Trimming the beard or nails is similar to shaving and hence prohibited, as it removes dishevelment (tafath). Tafath is defined as dirt and excessive hair/nails. Wearing garments dyed with wars (a plant), saffron, or safflower is prohibited for the muhrim; using them as a pillow or sleeping on them is also not allowed. The passage then poses a question: is it disliked for a non-muhrim man to wear such dyed clothes? It cites a hadith where the Prophet forbids wearing pure red, calling it the dress of the devil. The commentator notes the chain of transmission and its weakness. The passage ends mid-sentence.

Key Terms
التفث (al-tafath): Here defined as the dirt and dishevelment from long hair and nails, and its removal (qada' al-tafath) includes cutting hair, shaving the head, trimming nails, plucking armpit hair, and shaving pubic hair.
طيب (tib): Perfume - any substance used for its fragrance. The muhrim must avoid applying it directly, but wearing a garment that has been perfumed (e.g., by incense) is permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a muhrim wearing a garment that has been perfumed by incense?
A) It is haram because it involves perfume.
B) It is permissible because the garment is not used directly for perfume.
C) It is makruh tanzihi.
D) It is wajib to avoid.

Key Takeaway
The muhrim must avoid direct acts of covering, perfuming, and removing hair, but indirect exposures like scented garments are permissible, with some acts being merely disliked rather than sinful.

intermediate

Prohibition of Dyed Clothing for Muhrim and Red Dye for Men
Ruling on wearing dyed clothes and the special case of red dye

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibited dyes for a muhrim and explain why red dye is makruh tahrimi for non-muhrim men according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Wearing red is the devil's dress – prohibited for muhrim and disliked for all men.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah combines two rulings: what dyes a muhrim must avoid, and a separate prohibition on red clothing for all men. The author uses a hadith to extend the ihram ruling to a general etiquette. We'll examine the evidence and the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited dyes for a muhrim
Read the matn: wars (yellow), za'faran (saffron), 'usfur (safflower). Note that the prohibition extends to using such cloth as a pillow or sleeping on it.
These are scented dyes that violate the ihram prohibition of perfume.
2
Understand the extension to non-muhrim men
The commentator asks whether the ruling applies to non-muhrim men and answers by citing a hadith about red (humra). This shows that red is disliked for all men.
The hadith is from Ibn 'Umar, recorded in al-Tabarani.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The Prophet explicitly forbade wearing red and called it 'the dress of the devil.' In Hanafi usul, a clear prohibition (nahy) indicates tahrim (forbidden) unless there is evidence to lower it to karahah tahrimiyyah.
The Hanafi view is that it is makruh tahrimi for non-muhrim men because the hadith is ahad and the prohibition is not absolute.
4
Note the exception for washed garments
The text adds 'except if it is washed and does not exude (scent/dye).' The preferred interpretation is that it refers to scent; if no scent remains, the garment is permissible.
This exception applies to both muhrim and non-muhrim contexts.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school permits red for men as long as it is not pure silk. The Hanafi school is stricter on this point.
The ḥadīth is interpreted differently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا يلبس ثوباً مصبوغاً ،بورس، ولا بزعفران، ولا بعصفر). ولا ينبغي له أن يتوسده، ولا ينام عليه. وهل يكره لبسه لغير المحرم من الرجال؟ روي قال : أن ابن عمر نهاني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن لبس الحُمْرة، وقال: إياكم والحمرة، فإنها زي الشيطان»(۱). (1) معجم الطبراني الكبير ١٤٨/١٨ ، قال الهيثمي في مجمع الزوائد ١٣٠/٥ : رواه الطبراني بإسنادين في أحدهما : يعقوب بن خالد بن نجيح البكري العبدي، ولم أعرفه، وفي الآخر: بكر بن محمد يروي عن سعيد عن شعبة، وبقية رجالهما ثقات، ورواه في الأوسط، وفيه أبو بكر الهذلي، وهو ضعيف. اهـ، وقال العلامة : إلا أن يكون غسيلاً لا يَنْقُض . قوله: (إلا) أن يكون غسيلاً لا يَنفُض): أي لا تفوح رائحته، وهو الأصح ، وقيل : لا يتناثر صبغه
His statement: (And he should not wear a garment dyed with wars, nor with za'faran, nor with 'usfur). And it is not proper for him to use it as a pillow or sleep on it. And is it disliked (makruh) for non-muhrim men to wear it? It is narrated that Ibn 'Umar said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade me from wearing red, and he said: 'Beware of red, for it is the dress of the devil.' (1) (1) Mu'jam al-Tabarani al-Kabir 18/148, al-Haythami said in Majma' al-Zawa'id 5/130: Al-Tabarani narrated it with two chains, in one of them is Ya'qub ibn Khalid... [footnote continues]. Except if it is washed and does not exude (color/odor). His statement: (Except if it is washed and does not exude): i.e., its scent does not diffuse, and this is the most correct; and it is said: its dye does not shed.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It begins with the matn's prohibition: a muhrim must not wear a garment dyed with wars (a yellow dye), za'faran (saffron), or 'usfur (safflower). This prohibition extends to using such cloth as a pillow or sleeping on it. The commentator then raises a question: Is this ruling also disliked (makruh) for non-muhrim men? The answer is provided through a hadith: Ibn 'Umar reports that the Prophet forbade wearing red (humra) and called it the dress of the devil. This indicates that red dye is strongly disliked for men in general. The commentator adds an exception: if the garment has been washed so that no dye or scent exudes (i.e., it does not stain or emit fragrance), then it is permissible. The preferred opinion is that 'la yanfud' means it does not give off scent; another view is that it does not shed dye.

Key Terms
الورس (al-wars): A type of plant used to produce a yellow dye; prohibited for muhrim to wear.
الزعفران (al-za'faran): Saffron, a yellow-orange dye and fragrance; prohibited for muhrim.
العصفر (al-'usfur): Safflower, a plant yielding red or yellow dye; prohibited for muhrim.
الحمرة (al-humra): The color red; forbidden by hadith for men generally, not just muhrim.
غسيلاً لا ينقض (ghasilan la yanqud): A washed garment that does not exude dye or scent; an exception to the prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a non-muhrim man wearing a garment dyed with red (humra) according to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage?
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Disliked (makruh) because the Prophet called it the dress of the devil
C) Forbidden (haram) for all men
D) Only disliked if the dye is from saffron

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of red for men is established by an authentic hadith, making it makruh tahrimi, while muhrim must avoid any scented or dyed garment.
